Xalapa, Ver. ‚Äì Veracruz se ubica en tercer lugar a nivel nacional en la comisi√≥n de delitos como secuestros, homicidio doloso, extorsi√≥n, robo a negocio, trata de personas, narcomenudeo, violaci√≥n, feminicidio y robo a transe√∫nte.El almirante Eduardo Redondo Ar√°mburo, Subsecretario de Marina, dio a conocer que dichos delitos son los que mayor impacto tuvieron en la entidad durante el mes de febrero.Indic√≥ que el total de delitos contabilizados entre enero y febrero en la entidad fue de 3 mil 927, reflejando una ligera tendencia a la baja, respecto a los a√±os anteriores.

https://mexiconewsdaily.com/news/coronavirus/third-wave-of-covid-on-the-way-long-weekend-fills-streets-packs-beaches/
Coronavirus
A popular beach in Veracruz on the weekend.
Third wave of Covid on the way? Long weekend fills streets, packs beaches
Published on Monday, March 15, 2021
New coronavirus cases have declined significantly since Mexico went through its worst month of the pandemic in January but a resurgence of the national outbreak is not out of the question after people flooded streets and flocked to beaches over the weekend.
Average daily case numbers declined 28% to 5,668 during the first 14 days of March compared to February and were 60% below the average in January, a month in which Mexico recorded more than 438,000 confirmed cases and almost 33,000 Covid-19 deaths.
Perhaps believing that the worst of the pandemic is over and that the risk of infection is now substantially reduced, hordes of people descended on Mexico City‚Äôs historic center over the long weekend (Monday is a public holiday for the anniversary of former president Benito Ju√°rez‚Äôs birthday) while thousands headed for the beach in states such as Guerrero, Veracruz, Yucat√°n and Sinaloa.
In the capital, where the coronavirus risk level remains at orange light high on the federal government stoplight map, residents and visitors were out in force on Sunday, many strolling carefree down Calle Madero, a pedestrian street that runs between the Palace of Fine Arts and the z√≥calo, Mexico City‚Äôs central square.
Restaurants and shops downtown were also busy in stark contrast to the long red light maximum risk period the capital endured from the middle of December to the middle of February.
‚ÄúThere are more people, it must be because of the long weekend,‚Äù a policewoman told the newspaper El Universal. ‚Äú‚Ä¶ I think they don‚Äôt care about the pandemic or they think that it will be over in a few months.‚Äù
The city‚Äôs stoplight color and authorities‚Äô warnings about the ongoing risk of infection mean nothing to many people, she added.
Also taking advantage of the long weekend despite the pandemic were throngs of beachgoers in destinations such as Acapulco and Zihuatanejo in Guerrero, the port city of Veracruz, Progreso and Celest√∫n in Yucat√°n and Mazatl√°n in Sinaloa.
The newspaper Reforma reported that many people failed to observe social distancing recommendations while enjoying the sand and sea.
Guerrero Governor H√©ctor Astudillo said in a video message that there was a ‚Äúnotable‚Äù number of visitors in the state‚Äôs two main coastal destinations ‚Äì where hospital occupancy was around 50% ‚Äì and warned tourism sector businesses to remember that the risk of infection remains ‚Äúvery real.‚Äù
He also said he was lobbying the federal government to ramp up vaccination efforts in Guerrero before the upcoming Easter vacation period.
Crowds of pedestrians on Calle Madero in Mexico City.
In Mazatl√°n, hotel occupancy over the weekend was 75% to 80%, according to local hotel association representative Jos√© G√°mez Valle.
‚ÄúThere were beach hotels with 90% occupancy,‚Äù he said, explaining that many people took a last-minute decision to have a short break on the Sinaloa coast.
‚ÄúMazatl√°n was packed yesterday [Saturday] and today [Sunday] as well,‚Äù G√°mez told the newspaper Noroeste.
‚Äú‚Ä¶ Next weekend is also looking good,‚Äù he said, adding that the influx of visitors is ‚Äúgood practice for Holy Week.‚Äù
Indeed, some businesses in Mazatl√°n need to improve their observance of health protocols as a number of them, including restaurants, were observed in violation of basic measures designed to stop the spread of the coronavirus, which has sickened at least 2.1 million Mexicans and officially claimed the lives of about 195,000, figures widely considered to be vast undercounts.
With the start of Holy Week just two weeks away, Health Ministry official Jos√© Alom√≠a took the opportunity at Sunday night‚Äôs coronavirus press briefing to warn that Mexico could see a new, large coronavirus outbreak if mobility increases and people don‚Äôt follow measures to stop the virus‚Äôs spread.
The director of epidemiology said that the reduced risk level in many states ‚Äì
‚Äì doesn‚Äôt mean that people should go back to living their lives as they were before the onset of the pandemic just over a year ago.
‚ÄúWhile there are people who haven‚Äôt gotten sick, in other words people susceptible to infection, ‚Ä¶ we can have new outbreaks,‚Äù Alom√≠a said.
‚Äú‚Ä¶ And if there are new outbreaks ‚Ä¶ we‚Äôre going to have seriously ill people who require a general hospital bed or a bed with a ventilator and unfortunately we‚Äôre going to have people who die due to [Covid-19] complications,‚Äù he said.
Alom√≠a urged people not to drop their guard and recommended that people stay at home over Easter and not attend extended family gatherings.
‚ÄúWe want to invite the public to have a calm Holy Week, ‚Ä¶ celebrate [only] with close family and avoid infections in that way,‚Äù he said.
Covid-19 vaccines continue to be rolled out across many parts of the country but based on current indications it will at least be several months, if not longer, before Mexico reaches the level of immunity in the population required to bring the pandemic to an end.
About 4.3 million vaccine doses had been administered as of Sunday night, according to Health Ministry data, mainly to health workers and seniors.
and only 0.5% of the population is fully vaccinated, meaning that they have had both of the required shots of one of the four vaccines that have been used here since inoculation began on December 24.
Some health experts estimate that 70% to 90% of the population needs to be inoculated or infected with the virus to reach herd immunity. For that to occur, a minimum of around 90 million Mexicans ‚Äì the country‚Äôs population is just over 126 million ‚Äì would need to have Covid-19 antibodies generated either by infection or inoculation.
, with at least tens of millions more still susceptible, Mexico‚Äôs pandemic ‚Äì one of the worst in the world ‚Äì looks unlikely to end any time soon.
